  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d569a142-cd5a-44fa-ab90-ff51c1da5889'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText12986206561278605899" style="display:none">FANNNNNGGGGG! So, I loved Fang in this book but then when he kissed that girl and Max saw I was like "HOW COULD YOU?!?!??!"<br /><br />LOL, sorry, just had to get that out.<br /><br />Let's talk about the book in no specific order!!!<br /><br />- Iggy on the cover=HAWT!<br />- Fang and Max=HELL YEAHZ!<br />- Isn't it obvious that Nudge likes Fang<br />- These fakes names of theirs. XD Captain Terror all the way.<br />- Starting to dislike Angel.<br />- Remember when Iggy was crying? Didn't you feel so bad?!!?! I felt so bad for Iggy, I just wanted to <br /> hug him and other cutesy stuff.<br />- That woman in the suit. I'm not gonna say her name because I'm not sure I trust her yet...<br />- The ending was so abrupt to me.<br />- All the characters hairs grow so fast!!!<br />- Fang is so sexy with his new look. I'm jealous of Max.<br />- Do to a couple of things, I did not give this book 5 stars like I did with the first two books.<br />- Iggy doesn't look as hot with his new look but he still is so hot.<br />- Ari is ALIVE!!?!?! Wah?!!?!<br />- HAHA, that kid who jumped off the jungle gym and fell down, I laughed.<br />- I don't like swans.<br />- Arial, Jeff, Max, Nick and Dypher? Grrr....<br />- What would Max and Fang's pet name be?<br />- Captain Terror!!! HAHAHHA Still can't get over that... XD<br />- MAX'S EVIL TWIN!??!?!? <div id="review_971435168" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Kendra Marie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27336090-kendra-marie"><img alt="Kendra Marie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478645718p2/27336090.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer4063994935531919918">One of my favourites! Because who wouldn't want a world with 98% human and 2% avian mutants to be real?? No joke, I think it would be so cool for that to happen...         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2171836038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15216775608571319810">The book I read was Maximum Ride, Vol.3 and this book was written by James Patterson. The Genre of the book is fantasy. The book was mainly about how they went to go visit some of the kids homes, but they didn't find anybody at the homes. Then the erasers hurt fang and they had to go to the hospital, Then the FBI investigated them and they went to go live with one of the agents and the group went to school.   <span id="freeText15216775608571319810" style="display:none">The book I read was Maximum Ride, Vol.3 and this book was written by James Patterson. The Genre of the book is fantasy. The book was mainly about how they went to go visit some of the kids homes, but they didn't find anybody at the homes. Then the erasers hurt fang and they had to go to the hospital, Then the FBI investigated them and they went to go live with one of the agents and the group went to school. The book isn't mainly about the power of love, but it is about judging a book by its cover because if you do judge the book by its cover you might not like it but if you don't you might like it.<br> <br> The beginning of the book was mainly about how they went to go see their parents, but they didn't find their parents at the addressees. In the middle of the book was mainly about how they were attacked by the erasers, so they took fang to the hospital for him to get fixed. Then the FBI started to investigate the group. The end of the book was mainly about how they went to go live with one of the FBI agents, and they spend the rest of the time living at the agents house. They also started to go to school when they started to go live with agent.<br> <br> I really liked this book, and I really liked a lot about the book, except for some parts. Some of my favorite things about the book was that how you can see more of their powers in the book. I also like how they actually go live with the FBI agent and go to school. The thing I didn't like was that how they don't go see all the addressees of their parents house. The narrator wrote the book really well because it really explained what was going on in the text and you always new what happened. The book connected to the real world by making it so they have to go to school like every normal kid in the world.<br><br>I really liked the book and I really liked how the author wrote the plot of the book. I gave the book a 4 because I think he answered enough questions to make it a 4, but I don't think he answered enough to be a 5. I think this would be a good book for someone to read and I think they would like it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512150742i/24578583._SX540_.jpg" alt="Related image" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2774742339" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2774742339" />
    <a title="Emma Oertle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63644519-emma-oertle"><img alt="Emma Oertle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483926083p2/63644519.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2774742339?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Oertle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Oertle" href="/user/show/63644519-emma-oertle">Emma Oertle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2774742339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2959938147375509671">Maximum Ride is definitely a series I would recommend to others, whether they like comics or stories. Although I didn’t start the series with first book, I could already grasp how the story would go and the art style is something to admire as well. Just reading the third book in the story, makes you feel a close connection to the characters. You worry for their safety and get very hopefully that they’ll win. This book, manga, is about a group of outcasts, who were experimented on, and given wing</span>
  <span id="freeText2959938147375509671" style="display:none">Maximum Ride is definitely a series I would recommend to others, whether they like comics or stories. Although I didn’t start the series with first book, I could already grasp how the story would go and the art style is something to admire as well. Just reading the third book in the story, makes you feel a close connection to the characters. You worry for their safety and get very hopefully that they’ll win. This book, manga, is about a group of outcasts, who were experimented on, and given wings like angels. Many people, good and bad, are going after them, trying to capture them and study them. The group is made up of very young kids and older kids who look after the younger ones. They were said to be birthed by regular human parents, but had genes implanted before they were even born. As the kids were born, the doctors and scientists who put the different genes into them, lied to their parents, telling them that they were dead. The kids were then locked up and kept in cages, experimented on. They do later escape from the place they once trusted and fly around too different cities, and towns, to try and find their real parents. They eventually have to go to the hospital for one of the kids in the group gets hurt. They end up living with one of the people investing them, but she treats them very kindly, like they are her own. They go to school every day, although some of the kids don’t want to. After awhile, living with the FBI agent, they find out they are being watched and run away from the home they were given. The erasers and still after them and now that Fang has healed from injuries, they can move on to a different place without having to worry about him. The flock continue their journey to search for their human parents. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2959938147375509671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The bird-like kids are trying to blend in with a normal school and pretending to be like their classmates which obviously was not an easy task. This has Iggy on the cover, yet, he had a short-lived part in the graphic novel. Unsure why he was featured if you ask me. He had a panic attack moment of losing the team, all in his head, and then back to normal. <br /><br />It was just an okay read. 2.25 stars. <br /><br />Leisure read in 2018.<br /></span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_10854410'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10854410-witch-wizard"><img alt="Witch &amp; Wizard: The Manga, Vol. 1" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1458516358l/10854410._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('X3IpKqbYuB5mYyKhtkXxnbT7k+IprcwJH0FVGK98xDZkcKqlKWojZYd62g0w9i36sIvI0yap+VVHYCugSaO4GQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MiXMwfSz4BVvVqVmCLHtslydDkfGCKgHLhESQhudgtgJJ09OewF7bo5PXcqOAjHVWO1VdskMnVt2MGz6/UL+9w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
